<Author>RoseAlee
<Content>What a Gem! Last December American Airlines had a $250 Austin/San Juan round trip special that we couldn't pass up and pushed the Buy button! I mentioned the cheap airfare and our friends (other retirees) said we're in. With a little research we decided to circumnavigate the island staying at paradors and sample the fine Porto Rican food and the rums. What a great idea! I booked our rooms via Expedia.com at $107+tax/room/night. This was our last night in Puerto Rico. This is a very nice boutique hotel, that has little parking - maybe room for 5 cars. Regardless, it is nice and where they got 2 1/2 stars is beyond me. Through some type of mixup they did not have our reservations and were going to put us in a different upgraded hotel. However, upon showing our paid receipt from Expedia and stating that we did not want to stay in a differenc hotel from our friends, they upgraded us to a room near the bar. It had a four poster bed, small but complete kitchen and a sitting area. Everything was well kept and clean. I like these small hotels and can definitely recommend staying at the Wind Chimes. It's also easy walking distance to the more active area of San Juan.This cheap trip ended up being cheap as far as airfare and hotel cost, but be assured that we made up and more of the savings on fine food and drink. A great spur-of-the-moment trip. The best part of Puerto Rico is away from San Juan and amongst the locals in the countryside.Larry  Kelly

<Author>MinnesotaTravelBug_4
<Content>Wonderful Little Inn--Highly Recommended I found At Wind Chimes Inn in the Que Pasa? magazine--a publication about touring Puerto Rico, which is very helpful! I checked it out online and loved their website, checked reviews on here and was even more excited. I called to book a room and was told that there was only an economy room left or a large king-size room (which was out of our budget). We'd been hoping for a queen, but settled for the economy. When we got to the Inn, we were so surprised and pleased to find we'd been upgraded to the KING room for the same price of the economy! It was so nice of them to do that and made us love them even more! The place is so very cute and nicely decorated. It is clean and feels just like you're staying at your grandma's (or whoever else makes you feel like you're right at home). It is located just two blocks from the beach and near great dining. There is off street parking---which is a little bit of a small area and costs extra--but we felt that our rental was safe. This place has a lot of character and we were treated with nothing but kindness! We hope to come back annually! The best thing is that it is a very classy place for a very affordable price. We're on a student budget and yet we were able to stay here--and comfortably!

<Author>Christina_and_Brian
<Content>Not bad, but not the best This is definitely a quaint place to stay for couples. I recently booked my first trip to Puerto Rico with my boyfriend and we chose At Wind Chimes Inn due to all of the reviews we read online. We stayed from 9/24 - 9/28/2008. Its cute in the fact that it feels like home. When we arrived we were greeted by Felix, a very nice man at the front desk. He gave us a map and even took the time to explain to us what the best places to eat (where they served authentic Island food) and which buses to take to travel around. The hotel room we stayed in was up on the 2nd floor, back by the bar, Room 127. The room had a very comfortable Queen Sized bed, but overall it was a bit small and had a strange smell to it, somewhat like a musky odor. Its not that bad though. The AC worked fine, and you definitely need it for the heat! The bathroom could have been a bit cleaner, and the cable connection on the small tv in our room was really bad. There was a bit of a mosquito issue in the room, we kept the windows closed but for some reason, they just kept on coming in. The overall atmosphere of the hotel is great, makes you feel right at home. It is definitely nothing flashy and extreme. Outside of our room was a small sitting area where we enjoyed beers (Medalla Light is the best - try it!) and great music from the bartender just downstairs. The location is pretty good, literally one block from the beach. The walk to rest of the area is not too far either, just steps away from restaurants. The hotel is in a very quiet location, so if you're looking for relaxation, this is the perfect spot you want to be in. Otherwise, try and get a hotel a little bit closer to the Action in the heart of the Condado area, like the Marriot. The pool was clean and very nice as well. There is a really cute cat that we named Ferdinand that lingers around the patio and bar area outside. The Condado beach is really nice because its never too packed, but the waves are a bit on the strong side. If you keep heading towards the Old San Juan area, just before the Dos Hermanos bridge, there is a really beautiful beach with calm clear waters too.

<Author>laschus
<Content>A delightful, affordable gem A trip to San Juan was set as a birthday present for my girlfriend, and I wanted to find a place that would be fun and enjoyable without spending too much. I could tell by the squeal of delight she let out when she got into the room ahead of me that I hit my mark.Decorated in festive carribean motifs, the rooms at At Wind Chimes gave a feel of authenticity without going overboard. The stone tile floor was a bit much as it was uncomfortable to walk on, but on the whole the interiors were very delightful and exceedingly comfortable for the price. Our trip was, unfortunately, during a heavy rainy season and we didn't get out as much as we would have liked but the room gave us a pleasant and comfortable base to return to. We found the staff to be very helpful, including loaning us an umbrella for the day to protect us from the inclement weather. The proximity to the beach was very convenient and it is within a short bus ride to the center of the bustling Condado area. The only down side was the extremely limited parking area available within the neighborhood, and paying for parking in their very small lot meant having to shuffle automobiles to get out and about. Still, that was a small price to pay for a wonderful and affordable stay.

<Author>AZJOHN1
<Content>nice location, laid back feel After reading so many concerns about the property, I decided to see it for myself before committing. I stayed at the Embassy Suites (Isla Verde/Carolina...reviewed separately) upon first arriving and asked to see a room at Windchimes. Everything at the property (room, plumbing, pool, etc.) was in good condition, and I found some of the criticisms listed here to be harsh and/or exaggerated. The 2nd floor water pressure was adequate, and there was always hot water for me. I bathe at dinner time. Maybe it's different if you are showering in the morning along with lots of other people. I paid $85 for a standard (queen) room and later had to move to a king size room for $125 a night. This is off-season. The people who complain about the price being too high apparently don't know what rooms are going for at the chain hotels in town ($175 and up, with huge amounts of tax and resort fees added on.) The atmosphere is casual and quiet. There are lovely sitting areas, some sunny and others cozy and covered. The rooms are small, but I was no happier in the large room compared to the smaller one. I stayed just above the lobby and did hear some noise on occasion. The air conditioner or fan masked the noise, though. I can see how the rooms right next to the lobby would be noisy. After a few days, I noticed there are tiny cameras everywhere on the property, which is good for security, I guess. The free wi-fi usually did not work in the room, only in the lobby and bar, but the clerks were upfront about this. The location is great. I like to walk, and if you walk a block south, you are on a main street of a real local neighborhood. A block north, you're at a nice beach. A lot of restaurants, casinos, hotels, shops, etc. were about a 1/2 mile west. If you don't like to walk, then you probably will have to choose between the erratic bus service or expensive taxis. There's no entertainment or shopping right there. Most people say you should rent a car in San Juan, but traffic is a nightmare; parking is worse.

<Author>TravelingButterfly
<Content>Great location to the beach I definitely agree with the reviewer below me. It's a great location to the beach, but it's a good 15 minute walk to get to the main strip where the restaurants are. The bus is the BEST bet to get to Old San Juan - it's just 75 cents, but they only come every 20-30 mins. A cab is about $13-14.We had our reservation at the At Wind Chimes, but like a lot of people, got upgraded to the Acacia - which, in my opinion, was MUCH nicer!! We got a FREE upgrade, mind you, with a gorgeous balcony suite. There is zero parking on the street, nor do they have a parking lot (the At Wind has a lot for $10 a day, not worth it IMO). Definitely get any advice from FELIX at the front desk (Acacia) - he can recommend eateries, things to do, what to avoid, etc. Definitely go to Kasalta bakery for breakfast (10 min walk, opposite way of the Old City). And unlike a previous post, skip Bebo's cafe (it's Bebo's not Beso's). It's Dominican owned, and they have the WORST service ever. The food wasnt even worth it. Going into Old San Juan - eat at Lupi's Mexican Restaurant - so good!!!!I thought the rooms were really nice, we stepped out and had the jacuzzi right by our room. The pool is at the At Wind (you have access to both hotels) and the sandwiches and chips/salsa are excellent at the bar! You MUST go to the waterfall (El Yunque) - if you rent a car it's only a 25 min ride. I dont know how much a cab is. It's not far though.

<Author>Travellifenow
<Content>Cool Little Affordable Spot if Your Focus is Beach I stayed with a friend a few weeks ago and had a decent stay. The highlights were the staff was friendly and helpful, the cozy atmosphere of the inn, and I loved the acerola (cherry juice) that they had at the bar. The rooms were clean, although I didn't love the shower solution. You should definitely bring shower shoes. The biggest plus was the proximity to a nice stretch of beach. If my goal was to really get solid beach time - I would stay there again, especially if I was going it alone. The challenge is that in terms of location to Condado's restaurants and main strip - it isn't that close. You'll definitely do a 15/20 minute walk, cab for $8 minimum, or the bus. The cab and bus can be easy (front desk calls cab - and they come in like 3-5 minutes), the bus schedule is hit or miss. So overall - if I wanted to explore more restaurants or be closer to Old San Juan, I'd stay nearer to the Marriott or Condado Plaza. Other than that - it was a great find - you get what you pay for, but this was worth it, and a good intro to Puerto Rico.

<Author>MyaniqueD
<Content>Cute Inn My best friend and I stayed at Wind Chimes Inn during an impromptu vacation. We decided on Puerto Rico since we hadn't visited that island yet. (We travel through the caribbean quite a bit). We needed somewhere clean, near to the beach, with good staff and as inexpensive as possible. Wind Chimes was pretty good in all these areas. The room we stayed in was about the size of a standard bedroom, located upstairs w King Size bed and a bathroom. The water pressure wasn't that great, i guess because we were upstairs, and the hot water was intermittent. That wasn't a problem for us because this is a pretty standard situation in the caribbean unless you're in a big hotel. Bathroom was fairly clean, and our towels and linens were changed daily. Cable TV available in the room, and my friend picked up the internet on her laptop. The swimming pool is really just there to wade around and cool off in. Very small, but i liked it. There is a separate tanning area above the pool as well.The staff is awesome, we found ourselves hungry late one night and the chef/bartender Angel fixed my friend a tasty vegetarian pizza and i had a chicken quesadilla. AWESOME!!!The front desk staff is also really helpful with area information. The hotel is literally a block from the beach. The Condado beach is choppy and the sand isn't as nice as you would find in Negril, Jamaica but for Puerto Rico it was ok. Isla Verde beach is much nicer and not as many teeny boppers about. There were good restaurants to choose from. A five minute walk takes you to a Dominican Restaurant called Beso's. The french eatery La Patisserie was also excellent, the Quiche was amazing. Although my friend insists that the lunch meats there gave her a virus. (I recommend eating cooked meats in foreign countries...newho). 10 -15 minute walk takes you to a wide array of other eating areas, including Uno's Pizza, Starbucks, and other selections.We followed the suggestion to take the bus to Old San Juan and that worked out well for us, since we didn't feel like spending the extra money for a cab.Be prepared to be disappointed with the Bacardi tour, personally had I known what i do now, I would have skipped it. Basically you get 2 drink vouchers, then you take a trolley to the 'tour', Which is essentially videos and pictures, and then you get sent over to a drink expert who tells you how to make Mojito's, Cuba Libre and Daiquiri's. Then it;s over to the gift shop. That's it. No tour of the actual facility or taste testing or view of the estate.All in all, i would recommend Wind Chimes for singles, laidback, adventurous, flexible persons.

<Author>Louie74
<Content>Wanted to love it---but didn't. I was so excited to book this place, since I only read good reviews, but I was very disappointed in our room. It was very clean but ended up being the size of a postage stamp, the bed literally filled the whole room. We packed light, only two carry-on bags each for the two of us, but there was no place to put them. We had to stack everything on a chair in the corner and after 6 days the cramped space got very old. After a couple of nights we asked if there was anything else available and they said no, even though it was the middle of the week and we just saw a handful of people throughout our whole stay, but since we were in beautiful Puerto Rico, we weren't in the mood to argue. On the up side, the location was completely safe, we walked everywhere and stayed out on the beach til midnight every night without any problems. We also found a great place for breakfast called Kasalta, it's more like a bakery than a restaurant, but very good. The staff may recommend Pinky's, but we say nooo way. Everything just felt not right about that place, and I'm all about eating from vendors and kiosks, but that place was way too dirty feeling. So enjoy Puerto Rico, it was our first visit and we loved it!! If you don't mind extremely tight quarters I guess you should stay at Wind Chimes, but it really isn't worth the money.

<Author>skipus
<Content>Great time At Wind Chimes Just returned from Puerto Rico and six nights At Wind Chimes Inn as part of a group of about 25 people attending a wedding and reception in Old San Juan. This inn is a great place to stay if you want an alternative to the large resort hotel atmosphere while still being close to the beach (a five minute walk) and near many nice shops, restaurants and casinos. It is located in a residential neighborhood , and the whole property has a cozy BB feel to it. Although not overly friendly, the staff is competent and efficient (Felix at the front desk is the star of the group); the rooms are attractive, clean, but not luxurious, and a little smaller than some people may prefer. We don't spend a lot of time in the room, so it worked out perfectly fine for us; if you expect to do more than sleep, shower, and sit in rattan style chairs and watch TV or read a little after a busy day, you will probably be disappointed.The pool area and elevated sun terrace are near the street but a stone wall surrounds the area to provide some privacy. The boat bar a few steps away provides a welcome oasis with a limited menu (breakfast and lunch) and reasonable prices for food and drinks. The bar tenders were very friendly and the whole place has a very laid back, casual feeling to it.Unlike some other reviewers, our whole group did not feel nickel and dimed to death ; we felt they gave us good value for the prices they charged. Driving and parking in San Juan is a REAL CHALLENGE, so you might want to think twice about renting a car unless you plan on visiting other parts of the island. Although the cab fares do add up, it's the way to get around here if you go somewhere beyond walking distance. Public transportation is available and cheap, but we found it took a lot of time to get anywhere; service is a little erratic sometimes.All in all, we had a wonderful stay here. Be sure to visit their sister property down the street (the Acacia). Windchimes guests can take advantage of their huge hot tub area and fine restaurant.

<Author>eagle2435
<Content>Don't stay here in San Juan - I have another recommendation My wife and I were on our honeymoon for our Puerto Rico trip. We felt we paid too much for what we received. First of all, it seems like Wind Chimes Inn charges about 25% tax when everyone else on the island charges about 9%. We paid over $150 per night with taxes included when we only booked the room for $120 per night - do the math, that is a ton of taxes. We didn't know better though, because it was the first hotel we stayed in. The room was nicely decorated but pretty small - also, we were given a room right beside the lobby and the front door, even though we told the lady at check-in that we were on honeymoon and wanted some peace and quiet. This definitely caused some problems, what with the spring breakers slamming doors and yelling in the lobby til about 3:30 am every night and the hotel not doing anything to calm the freaks down. Nothing is complimentary and you WILL get nickel and dimed more than anywhere else. Also, the hot water seemed to be non-existent half of the time - take a quick shower if you stay here. It is close to the beach and shops and restaurants which is nice. Also - no parking unless you want to pay $10 per day, and it is pretty difficult to find a spot near the Inn. All in all, the Inn is clean and nicely decorated, but we felt it is overpriced and doesn't offer very good service or value. As a recommendation, we stayed at another hotel in San Juan called the Oceana Hostal Playero on the latter part of our trip and enjoyed a much quieter, nicer, and much less expensive stay. Hope this helps!

<Content>Reservations Don't Mean Much Don鈥檛 count on staying here just because you have reservations. We reserved four nights at the hotel many months ago, and were looking forward to staying here. We told her that we reserved four nights, but to no avail. She checked and checked and she was ever so sorry, but nothing was showing up, and there was absolutely nothing available except for that one night on the 14th. Considering that the hotel has a three day minimum stay policy it remains a mystery to us how we were booked for only one night when we reserved. But when we asked, we were told that the person who supposedly made the mistake when she reserved for us was no longer working there. The desk person did try to help us and called several other places to try to find us a room, as did the lady who I believe was the manager, but this being Valentine鈥檚 Day as well as President鈥檚 Day weekend preceding winter break and cruises for many people, there was absolutely nothing available in the price range similar to At Wind Chimes Inn. Finally we were able to find a room at the Condado Plaza (which I will review separately), but that meant that this vacation cost us more than twice as much as what we were originally counting on spending. And, as the icing on the cake, we had to spend another 14 dollars to take a second taxi to the Condado Plaza from this hotel, on top of the 16 from the airport to Wind Chimes.I think as a gesture to make up for the ineptitude in making reservations, they could have offered to pay for the second cab, or at the very least, offer us a drink on the house before we left for the Condado. But aside from 鈥渟o sorry,鈥?nothing was offered.So, my recommendation is to call and double check your reservations before you leave for the Wind Chimes Inn; don鈥檛 assume that just because you have reservations you will actually end up staying here.To be fair, I want to point out the terrible experience rating (one star) reflects only the lost reservation and stress of not having a room after a long day of travel. It does not reflect the hotel itself, such as rooms, restaurant, or service. For all we know, that may have been wonderful. We just didn't get to experience it.

<Author>lifesavermom
<Content>Good times at the wind chimes.... My husband and I and our two very young children stayed at the Wind Chimes Inn for four nights, January 29-Feb 2nd. It is a cozy, beautiful little hacienda in the heart of San Juan. Only a short walk to Condado beach. The staff are helpful and knowlegeable; anytime we needed something, they were there IMMEDIATELY. I have heard that some rooms are very small, tv's are small, etc. However, we had a beautiful King room with a decent sized tv and a little kitchenette. It was cozy and comfortable. There was a fold out futon for our 4 year old to sleep on, and the front desk staff immediately brought extra sheets and blankets for him. The food at the Boat Bar is very good, as are the drinks! It was easy to take a short walk to Bebo's Cafe, the bus stop, the beach or a drug store. I felt very at home at the Wind Chimes and would definitely stay there again. The only imperfections: our room was right next to the boat bar (as my husband says, the bar was in our living room--we actually had to walk through it to get to our room) and it got a bit noisy in the am for us 10am risers. The noise at night didn't bother us. Also parking is VERY limited; you can pay $10/night if you have a compact car to park in the tiny gated lot---but there is only space for 4 vehicles. Otherwise, you're fighting for space on the side street, which is no easy task. I loved the Wind Chimes and have wonderful memories there now. Will probably stay again on our next trip!I am in love with Puerto Rico.

<Author>theaj
<Content>Warmth and Charm at Wind Chimes! Wind Chimes had all the charm and warmth we were looking for in San Juan and was a good jumping off place for other island destinations. Located in a quiet Condado neighborhood just a block from the beach and a few minutes walk to restaurants and shopping, Wind Chimes is an excellent alternative to the noise and glitz of the tourist beat. Staff goes out of their way to be helpful and welcoming. Rooms are comfortable and clean. (Our king sized bed was amazingly sleepworthy!) The Boat Bar, serving delicious light fare all day long, is a convenient, palate-pleasing feature. Every one of the gifted gentlemen serving there made us feel like family! Nearby is the newly opened 'Niche' restaurant in Acacia, Wind Chimes' sister facility. Not only is the food there beautifully prepared and presented, but the decor is also a delight to the eye. Wind Chimes is great place to come back to -- we're already planning the next trip and would recommend it to anyone looking for a little home away from home in San Juan.

<Content>Adequate but I would not return. The staff is nice and the place is close to the beach, well maintainedand clean, but I found several things that I disliked: a) On arrival they charged our credit card for the eight days we were staying there.It felt like we were prisoners and could not change our minds if we did not like the place. There are tables on a second floor which are somewhat better but the serviceto these tables is mediocre at best. c) There are lots of additional charges: there is a tax on the breakfast bill that you only find out you have to pay on the last day, it is not included in the receipt yousign at breakfast each day. The chairs that you can take to the beach are $3. Whenever you call a taxi you pay a tourist fee which is much higher than what the meter shows. So, all additional expenses added together make this place as expensive as one of the good hotels closerto town and to the good beaches and restaurants. d) You are not reallyon Condado beach which is the nice beach. You are on a block from a beach that is mostly used by surfers and where very few people go swimming. e) The pool is small and receives little sun because there are several buildings that surround the house and keep the pool in theshade. f) The neighborhood has a few restaurants but the shops and themore commercial areas are not on walking distance. My suggestion is that you stay here only if you have a car and if you like large waves and surfing.

<Author>MspTripper
<Content>Enjoyed 3 nights here Enjoyed 3 days here before going to Culebra. The Condado location is very manageable, I took the bus into old San Juan my first day there. Condado Beach is a close block away. There are numerous restaurants in the area. The property itself is a nice little gem, very non-commercial in appearance and feeling. The boat bar is a nice place to have a drink or a solo dinner which I did the first night there. The 2 guys working behind the bar were great and my dinner, prepared as I watched, was delicious. We had probably the worst room in the hotel. It was the front room, with it's door opening off the tiny lobby and next to the front door. It was small, with a queen bed. The location next to the lobby was noisy in the evening and morning when people were coming and going or talking in the lobby. It had both a room a/c unit and a ceiling fan. In general the fan was sufficient to keep the room cool and had an added benefit of providing white noise to block out some of the lobby noise (unlike the a/c which was made the standard roar) The off-season rate, including taxes, was only $100 a night, which is cheap by San Juan standards.

<Content>So-So at Wind Chimes The hotel room was small but clean. <Author>MLR_2007
<Content>Beautiful, Comfortable and Cheap (in the off-season)! We thoroughly enjoyed our stay here! The hotel is gorgeous; charming, very clean and well-maintained. The pool is small, but really lovely with a little waterfall. There was only one staff member who was sort of lazy with her suggestions as to where to eat, etc., but everyone else was great. They helped us get on public transportation, moved our luggage for us, and were quick with recommendations. We agreed to change rooms twice. For five days we paid $75 per night for a large room, queen bed, separate seating area, and then stayed one night in a smaller room for the same price. This room was same as the first one but without the separate seating area. The last room we stayed in was huge, with a king bed and kitchenette; I believe that cost $130. The bar staff is great. They were friendly but not overly so, generous, and their food was delicious! They even make their own balsamic vinegar. And they sqeeze oranges right in front of you for any drinks you might order that contain orange juice. The bar is very quaint-looking -- it is open to the courtyard rather than being indoors.The beach is a block away from the hotel. When we were there it was pretty empty. The ocean was a little rough because at that point we weren't near a bay, nor were there any retaining walls. The hotel staff will probably recommend you eat at Bebo's, but there is a restaurant called Jataca that is across the street from BeBo's and a few steps down (to the west) that has great food for very cheap.All in all we had a wonderful time. We got to experience a less tourist-sanitized P.R. than one would experience staying in a Holiday Inn or on a resort.

<Author>airsonu
<Content>good location but small At Wind Chimes Inn in San Juan, Puerto Rico was in a good location in Condado, but in general the room was small, and the bathroom even smaller. We stayed 3 nights.Like other overdeveloped areas, the building looked like a well maintained converted bungalow. Parking space is a luxury. Nearby street parking might be available if you are lucky. Otherwise, the Inn has a driveway that can hold about 6 cars. Driveway parking is tight, and only if everyone parks carefully can entry and exit be made without moving another car.Our room was accessible through a narrow walkway at the rear of the building. There was no sunlight at all, and the door to another room was immediately adjacent to ours.The room was clean and well furnished with standard amenities. My only significant complaint was the bathroom. A corner of the room was blocked off with a diagonal wall and very thin closet door. This was the bathroom. It was very tight for a 5' 11 165 pound man. I think it was impossible to change clothes in there.Internet access was available but only in certain areas of the property. Since the building was constructed with bricks there was no signal in our room. We had to sit in the patio bar area for internet access.The patio bar area looked like it was meant for a small group of close friends to hang out at. I have no opinion one way or the other about it.There are many restaurants within a 10 minute walk of the Inn.The beach is within a 5 minute walk of the Inn. The beach was clean and not crowded. We didn't spend much time at the beach, so I can't say much about it.The beaches in the Carolina and Isla Verde areas are a short drive from the Inn.Access to main roads and highways was very good.In general the staff was helpful, but a couple front desk receptionists didn't speak English well enough to help us.Overall, because the room was small, I would not return to this Inn unless there were no other choices.

<Author>jerryandsusan32
<Content>Wonderful! My husband and I spent July 8 - July 12 at Wind Chimes and wish we had planned to stay longer. This is a beautiful inn in a lovely setting. Our room was very nice - yes, the bathroom is small but who cares when you're in such a great place. Also ask them for recommendations of restaurants, things to see and do, etc. Pamela's is wonderful for a special dinner. Now, to the one thing that sets At Wind Chimes totally apart from other lovely inns - THE BOAT BAR! <Author>BaechLover
<Content>Been twice and happy both times The Wind Chimes is great if you want to go to Peurto Rico and not spend a fortune on your accomodations. The parking can be a pain, this is an urban area, I would not recommend a car unless you really plan to go around the island. Tours are availble and well worth the price. The buzzer at the door is for your own safety. One person was diappointed that there was no room service, but the bar will bring your food to your room if you ask. I was skeptical of the bar's food at first sight, because it so small, but it was delicious. We have eaten breakfast, lunch, and dinner there many times, and it is always good. We stayed in room 120 both times, and for about $120.00 a night you have a private balcony, and a king sized bed. It is less than a full block to the beach, and it is also close to many restaurants. The front desk will help with cabs, or advice. We have stayed there twice, and would do so again.

<Author>HellertownTraveler
<Content>Quaint convenient location At Wind Chimes in San Juan was our first stop during a 10 day trip to PR. We stayed 3 nights and were quite satisfied. We had a nice upstairs room with a small outside seating area complete with wrought iron table and chairs. Our room had a king size bed (very comfortable mattress), big ceiling fan and air conditioning, plus a fridge. Room was cleaned daily. One short block from the beach which is wide with white sand. Ocean is beautiful, with waves. Beach wasn't crowded - definitely visit the beach while you're there.Staff was friendly and helpful. They gave us directions to places to eat withing walking distance. Try Bebos, it's a block and a half from the hotel, very reasonable - under $30 for dinner for 2, with drinks. I had rented our car in advance, from Thrifty (cheapest), before we arrived in San Juan. You jump in the Thrifty bus at the airport, and you are taken right to the car lot. You get your car and off you go. I reccomend renting a car, there's so much to see within a 45 minute drive from Condado - if you only make one trip out of San Juan, make it Luquillo Beach. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>HLSTravelers
<Content>Charming and Great for the Price All and all my boyfriend and I really enjoyed our stay but there weresome things people should be aware of. We booked a room in the At Wind Chimes Inn through Expedia but when we arrived they said that our room was in their other building down the street. This other building is a new hotel that's just opening called Acadiana so there was lots of construction going on. The parts of the hotel that were finished were absolutely gorgeous and it was closer to the beach thanthe at wind chimes (which is only a block from the beach). Even though we were in the Acadiana, we were able to use all the amenitiesof the At Wind Chimes Inn. We ended up not minding the switch but if you would mind, you should confirm which building you will be stayingin.The LOCATION is great! You are a block from the beach and only 10 minutes from downtown Old San Juan. It really is the best of both worlds. The neighborhood is quiet. If you go a block in one directionyou hit designer shops and fancy restaurants but a block in the otherdirection and the area is a little sketchy so be aware of that.The FOOD at the bar was amazing! They cook everthing right in front of you. It's really fresh and just wonderful. It's not super cheap but it's not super expensive either. The bar staff is friendly and welcoming as well. It can take a while if you get there when it's busy though.The POOL is small but a nice place to relax and if you want to swim in something bigger, the ocean is just a block a way. The BEACH nearby was not that crowded and had lots of great waves.I would definitely recommend the At Wind Chime Inn or the Acadiana (when it opens up as its own hotel). I can't wait to go back myself!

<Author>ponsib
<Content>Great place to stay in San Juan I stayed at Wind Chimes with my wife and two children (ages 6 and 9) for three nights. There is a three night minimum stay at the Inn. We arrived for a late check-in after the pool is normally closed. The front desk woman (I don't remember her name) offered to let the kids swim as long as their voices were down. The kids loved it! I asked her if I could still get food from the boat bar and she informed me that the food service was closed but she then walked over with me and asked the bartender what he could make for me. She really went out of her way to make us happy. Speaking of the boat bar, one of the workers is attending culinary school and I was impressed with his attention to details and the effort he made when making and serving the food. We also had great breakfasts (the pancakes are awsome but not on the menu) while listening to caribbean music. Everyone that we encountered at the Inn were pleasant to deal with. We found it very easy to catch a bus to Old San Juan from this location. I wouldn't recommend that you take a car to this area because parking and traffic is a mess. Our room had one bed with a futon for the kids to sleep on and was adjacent to the boat bar. It was nice to wake up in the morning and have our coffee at the small table just outside our door. The music at night was kept low and didn't bother us at all. I believe was turned off at 11pm. The room was nothing fancy but it served it's purpose well. I would stay here again if we travel back to San Juan without hesitation!!

<Author>moonshaker
<Content>Great Beach, great Location My wife and I stayed at Windchimes Apr 11-15, 07. The location was great, the beach was one of the best I have ever experienced. We were able to easily find out the popular eating places that the locals liked and the food was great. When we traveled to the ritzy section with the five star hotels, we found the tourist were snobby, the food was TOO Americanized and not at all as good as the small dining places. If you need pomp and glitz this is not it. .We ate three brekfast at the Pueblo grocery nearby - The food was so good. And don't forget about Pinky's just down the beach for lunch and Bebos for an outstanding dinner.  The Beach was not crowded and we were always able to get a nice place under the coconut trees to set up our beach chairs. The surf was a little rough but did not deter us from an ocassional swim. The Staff at Windchimes was very courteous and did all they could to be helpful. The food at the bar was excellent, drinks were great and the prices were resonable. Ask for a room off the front as the locals stay up late around the weekend and it may be a bit noisy at night - but not too bad.

<Author>haley01
<Content>At Wind Chimes was great! My boyfriend and I stayed here for 4 nights in mid-March. We had a great time. The staff members were all friendly and helpful. Our room (128) was great--we had our own private balcony with a table and chairs. The walk to the beach was not too long. We also used the spa at Acacia and really enjoyed it.The room was clean. We felt completely safe staying there, and even kept our valuables (including cash) in the room without using the safe and didn't have any problems. I was not comfortable doing that at first but my boyfriend asked Jeannie at the front desk about renting the safe and she said there was no need, the housekeepers had worked there for 15 years. She was right. My only complaints about the room are that there was no full length mirror and the shower was OK the first couple of times, but by the end of our stay I was wishing for my shower at home. Just not enough pressure for me, I guess. Also don't forget to bring your hair-dryer as there is not one in the room. We rented a car and parked on the street, as it was a last-minute decision and the parking lot was full. We had to drive around the block a few times, but other times we found a spot right outside the hotel. I'd rather save the $10 a day. We had breakfast at Kasalta a couple of times and it was really good--fresh pastries. Leave the hotel and go right, towards Ocean Park (within walking distance). We also ate at the Columbo Frozen Yogurt place in Condado one morning and that was surprisingly good as well--really good Cafe Con Leche. For dinner, we ate at Latin Star in Condado (good local food), Mirabueno in Old San Juan (great food--more upscale, and we happened to go on Opera Night which was a neat experience), and Pamela's in Ocean Park. Pamela's was my favorite, as we went a little later (9 pm or so) and had a table on the beach. It was really quiet out there, only about 8 tables. The food was really good--I had fish, my bf had lamb. We had snacks at the Boat Bar at the hotel a few times--the mango salsa was very good. We went drinking in Condado the first night and walked back to the hotel with no problems. We took a cab another night. We also took a cab into OSJ Saturday night. We went back during the day on Monday and drove our car and parked at a deck near the Sheraton. I also gambled a bit at the Sheraton in OSJ and the Marriott and had good luck at both. Very small though, not like Vegas casinos.Overall we had a great time at this hotel and in San Juan. Like many other reviews have said, if you are expecting luxury, stay somewhere else. But if you are looking for a beautiful, cozy inn with great rates, stay here!  
<Date>Apr 20, 2007

<Author>Minnesota_Ice
<Content>Excellent small inn. I happened on the Wind Chimes because I needed a place to stay when my flight was delayed because of snowstorm. I didn't expect to find such a treasure.The Wind Chimes is a perfectly appointed and renovated small hotel located on the border between the Condado (ritzy, beach, and high rises) and Ocean Park (ritzy, beach, and homes).The staff were exceptional. The facility includes a small pool, sundeck, and bar that serves a limited menu for all meals. The hotel is allied with (managed by? owned by?) the Acacia Guesthouse, which is half a block away and just finishing renovations. At this time, guests are allowed to use the common facilities at either hotel.The hotel is definitely gay-friendly and probably 25% of the clientele were gay couples.My room was nicely appointed, exceptionally clean, and a bargain at $80 plus tax for a queen size bed.I'll be back!

<Author>bartsbabe
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised! After reading some of the negative online reviews, particularly on this site, about Wind Chimes Inn, I was somewhat hesitant to stay there. However, my boyfriend and I took a chance and thoroughly enjoyed our stay! It is a wonderful, comfortable, affordable inn that feels like home away from home. We stayed 3 nights pre-cruise and we do not have kids.Here's a rundown of Wind Chimes Inn...Location-quick walk to the beach, restaurants, shopping, and only 10-15 minute drive to airport and cruise ships. We felt very safe walking around by the Inn and neighboring homes were all well kept.Parking- did not have to deal with since we always walked or took taxis.Doors to property- require your room key to enter and exit, but not a big deal and worth it to feel safe.Front desk staff- ALWAYS helpful and accommodating. Got to know each one a little bit.Rooms-Our room was wonderful. Very comfortable, cool, high ceilings, lots of room to put our stuff. The bathroom was on the small side, but that didn't bother us one bit.Public areas- The lobby is lovely and inviting. The upstairs terrace area with the wind chimes is a quiet place to enjoy a book. The sun deck has several big comfy lounge chairs. The courtyard is a great place to meet people and read.Pool- Not heated but it doesn't need to be! Very comfortable water temp. and the perfect place for a dip. No smaller than a lot of back yard pools!Bar/restaurant- Our favorite part! We spent a lot of time here chatting with the staff and other guests. The drinks were wonderful and the food was affordable and delicious! It was just so convenient to have this bar right inside the hotel and it made meals times very easy. Contrary to other reviews on this website, the bar staff does not make any of the food on a George Foreman Grill! Several of the bar staff members are studying culinary arts and prepare your food on open flames right in front of you. All of the food was beautifully presented and delicious. Worth EVERY PENNY!Overall- we just loved our time at Wind Chimes Inn and we were sad to leave. We highly recommend this place to anyone looking for a charming, affordable, friendly place to stay.

<Author>1SCREEN1NAME1
<Content>Great! At Wind Chimes Inn was exactly as pictured on its website - charming and clean. The staff was very friendly and helpful. The location was good - in the residential area of Condado, a 5-minute walk to the beautiful beach, and a 10-minute walk to the local bakery (there is an authentic bakery a few blocks east of the inn, in Ocean Park). You have to take a cab or drive to Old San Juan and to the nightlife in Condado (bars, casinos, restaurants). The cab ride to the nightlife in Condado was $8, or a 20-25 minute (sweaty) walk. We did not go to the inn bar and restaurant, but there were always people there, and we have heard that the food is good. Our room was perfect - the only one located on the top floor with the terrace. The terrace is open to the patrons, but no one goes up there. The only small downfall to the inn is the lack of parking in the parking lot - we saved $10, but had to park on a busy street a block away. We would stay at At Wind Chimes Inn again.

<Author>cdillard
<Content>Charming, pleasant staff We stayed here three nights in July. I would recommend the hotel for stays no longer than three nights, and for couples/singles without children: there isn鈥檛 much that children can walk to.Accommodations. Our room was in the back, past the boat bar. Accommodations were comfortable, slightly above basic. The ceiling fan made the room actually quite cool, even with the A/C turned to low. The bathroom door was slotted (like blinds) so there was almost no privacy. The shower had a curtain, but was otherwise open; the size of a tub. I agree with comments that the water takes awhile to warm up: let it run about five minutes before jumping in. The pool is small, but is great if you can snag it to yourselves (which isn鈥檛 hard to do).Staff. The staff was very friendly. They directed us to restaurants, the bus stop and the Pueblo. When it came time for us to venture beyond San Juan, they assisted us with a car rental and a flight back from Vieques. The man at the front desk was very informative about the flights, ferries and car rentals, providing us with information to help make our decision about transportation to and from Vieques. The beach is just one block from the hotel, and is not at all crowded. If you have a rental car while staying here, check with the hotel first (in advance) to find out if they have a parking space available (very limited parking). If not, you will have to park on the street鈥攁nd there is not much space on the street, either. For the one night we had our car at the hotel, we had to park illegally on the street, along with about a dozen other cars. There were no problems, but it made me nervous. Dining. Most of the Condado restaurants are about a mile up Ashford Avenue (which is called McLeary in front of the hotel). Bebo鈥檚 is a Puerto Rican cuisine restaurant a bit closer, about two blocks toward Condado on Calle Loiza. They are fairly inexpensive ($10pp) and seem to be quite popular with locals. Transportation. The A5 bus runs to Old San Juan for $.75/person each way. It picks up on Calle Loiza; ask the front desk to direct you. If you take a taxi back from Old San Juan, go to the Plaza Colon (in front of San Cristobal). There is a taxi stand here, and because it鈥檚 at the edge of town, you won鈥檛 have to sit in OSJ traffic. We took a taxi from Plaza Colon to At Wind Chimes Inn and it was $12.Location. The hotel is in a residential area, about a mile from the Condado strip. We made the walk after dark, but it made me a bit nervous at times.

<Author>graceCP
<Content>not fancy; but nice. My husband and I stayed at At Wind Chimes Inn in April 2006 ,for a total of 8 nights(7 pre-cruise and 1 post-cruise). We found the inn to be clean and the staff super-friendly. Gabby in reception was really helpful ,as well as Claudette. Juan at the bar was charming. Prices were reasonable. Although the nightlife is not exactly booming , it is a great place to relax at the end of the day. There is a great selection of drinks, and while the choice of food is limited, it is cooked right in front of you.If you are looking for a luxury hotel, this is NOT it. If you are looking for a reasonably-priced, clean hotel ,with a personal touch, then Wind Chimes fits the bill. (We paid approx.105.00 per night U.S.) The rooms are small but clean, and if you so choose you can rent the efficiency unit with a small fridge and chesterfield for more room(PRICED HIGHER AT APPROX 150.00)The towels are plentiful, the staff are courteous.The pool is small but great for a dip on a hot day. Most time is spent at the beach anyway so who cares? Old San Juan is just 10 or 15 minutes away by bus (fare is 0.75 cents each way). There is a great restaurant called Bebosthat serves chicken, burgers, etc,, with really reasonable prices. Also for those who want fast foods there is a Burger King, a MacDonalds, and a KFC within walking distance (10 min).We would definitely visit San Juan again. The people are fantastic and there is lots to see and do. Would we stay at Wind Chimes again??? Without a doubt!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disappointing From reading other reviews, it seems that the quality of the rooms can differ tremendously from room to room. I was looking at someone else's pictures on this site, and their room seems nicer, cleaner, and brighter than what we got. My husband and I chose to stay here for 5 nights because it was highly recommended by our guidebook as One of the most charming small inns on the island. The common areas--the lobby, the boat bar, the pool--are indeed charming, but our room was quite small, worn, and dark. The furniture was VERY worn and the air conditioner was loud and blew directly on us. Housekeeping was sketchy, and we even found some dead cockroach parts in the closet. It didn't seem like the sheets were changed at all the entire time we were there, and it didn't seem like the floor was swept very well either. Our room also didn't have a bathroom door (as in, it was not part of the architectural plans), and this was rather annoying. The shower temperature was hard to regulate and the drain was clogged. The room smelled very strongly of the bathroom cleaner that they used, and we were bit by mosquitoes in the room every night. We looked into changing hotels, but Wind Chimes wouldn't refund us the money for our unused nights, and it would've cost too much to pay in full here as well as at a new hotel, so we just stayed it out. On the plus side, the hotel is very close to the beach, so it made it convenient to go every day. It's a little far from downtown Condado, but it is very walkable and the walk is enjoyable. The staff is friendly (although they sort of messed up our rainforest tour) and accomodating. I don't know that we would stay here again.

<Author>sweetatlgirl
<Content>Charming Inn, Great Value We just spent three nights At Wind Chimes Inn and would definitely recommend it. The location is great, particularly if you enjoy a quiet more residential area. The Inn is out of the hustle bustle of Condado, but close enough to enjoy what the Condado has to offer and then return to a more relaxed pace back at the Inn. It is only a block from the beach and just a bit further to a nice neighborhood park. It is also close enough to walk to the Pueblo 24 hr. Supermarket and several excellent local restuarants. We found the Inn very comfortable with a nice laid back feel. The rooms were clean, great King bed - all the comforts of home. The only complaint I had was the room only had one chair, a second one would have been nice. The common areas were pleasant and we really enjoy having a drink at night out on the upper deck. It was an easy walk to Bebo's Cafe for dinner and we were completely comfortable walking back to the Inn at night. Bebo's, although lacking in atmosphere (it is a little bright) is a great value. It is definitely a local favorite, generally packed with what are obviously nearby residents - friends and families, young and old. They tend to give English menus to tourists but be sure to ask for one in Spanish as well - the daily specials are only in Spanish and they are a good deal - mostly $5 - $6. We ate there twice and everything was delicious. Cafe de Angeles on Ashford is also good - more atmosphere and an open air eating area but it is mostly tourists. However, it is quiet a walk from the Inn, but it's a great way to burn off all the Medella and Tostones. If walking isn't your speed you can always take the bus. We liked the B21 better than the A5 but be sure to have exact change (the front desk is happy to provide change) and remember you might have to wait quite a while for the bus, but it will show up eventually. The staff was friendly and helpful and I would be happy to stay here again.  
<Date>Dec 14, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Special Place - Great for a Restful Stay I visited At Wind Chimes Inn last month for a week, and had a delightful time. I can highly recommend At Wind Chimes Inn with only a few reservations. As for it's best qualities, the staff at the inn are very warm and helpful. They accommodated my every request, and were always just as nice as could be. Also, the fact that the inn is locked from the street creates a very comfortable atmosphere inside the place. There are various levels for resting, sunning, etc. so the quiet and leisurely atmosphere was just wonderful. Lots of deck chairs, so just pick your spot. Also, I really liked the bar area, where meals are served. I really enjoyed the omlettes and several times found myself having other meals there when plans changed, or I just couldn't decide where else I wanted to go. (Some of the restaurants in Condado get very crowded, and this wasn't even high season!) The bar staff was great and very professional. Nice tropical drinks, too. As it was off-season, the bar area was never crowded or even full--though, I think it would be even more fun with a bigger crowd. Far more chatty and personal than what the big hotels offer.The location of the inn is a plus, unless you want to be right in the thick of the tourist area, or perhaps in Old San Juan (which would be a more Old European-style vacation, in my opinion). It is located in a residential area, but the walk to the tourist area is only a few blocks. And a nice beach is indeed very close by. And the downtown area is not far in another direction. If you enjoy getting a bit away from things like me, this is perfect. The staff gave me a little map of the neighborhood that was very helpful.As for the negative, the only real complaint I had was that the air conditioning in my room was extremely noisy--honestly, it sounded like an outboard motor running. I quickly learned that I could not expect to leave it on and rest. Luckily, the rooms at Wind Chimes are dark and cool due to the building design (this is a plus when you come in from the hot sun), so I found that I could cool down the room with the AC before retiring, and leave it off for the night to sleep--it stayed fairly cool throughout the night. I have read descriptions that some A/C units at this inn are quiet--I would certainly request a quiet A/C before staying here again. My toilet also had a tricky handle, but this was a minor complaint. There are no hair dryers or shampoo, etc--so bring your own extras. (It's a shame that some low-cost extras could not be added because it would really enhance the stay.)Back to the positives--the tour guide, Captain Paul, who is associated with At Wind Chimes is unbelievably nice. I spent the day on one of his better tours--by myself, because some other parties had cancelled. Captain Paul is knowledgeable, friendly and helpful. He agreed to take my party of 1 anyway. I went horseback riding and to be bio-bay with him. I really loved the horseback riding--what a great ranch. The biobay was fascinating, though the kyacking to get to there was more work than I had anticipated. Captain Paul either stayed with me, or carefully explained where he would meet me after an activity. However, all in all it was a really wonderful day. Very memorable. I wished I had been there longer so I could have gone some other places with Captain Paul--next time, I think I'll ask for one of his city tours. I went to on a trip to Ponce, but regretted that I didn't have someone as helpful and nice as Captain Paul--this man was born to be a tour guide!San Juan is a different sort of vacation spot than many other places in the Caribbean, I am sure. It is more urban, with urban sprawl, but it has loads of delights, too, and qualities that make it very special. Old San Juan and the Forts are indeed an international treasure. So read up on how to get the most of your stay here--there are lots of terrific things to do. And the people I met were warm and friendly.I would definitely stay at At Wind Chimes again, and hope to be able to do so soon.  
<Date>Jul 7, 2005

<Content>Great Discovery For our first time to Puerto Rico, we looked to TripAdvisor for a place to stay. <Author>ChristineLuv2TRVL
<Content>Thumbs up for the Wind Chimes Inn I spent one night at Wind Chimes' new property, the Acacia, which is just down the street from the Wind Chimes Inn. The room was quaint, a little small, but beautifully and tastefully decorated. The beds were plush, as were the pillows. A very comfy bed. The Wind Chimes bar was superb. It was so nice to sit back and relax, have cocktails and snacks, then hit the pool/spa. The pool is small, but it sure cools you off. The next morning, I stopped by to order breakfast. Instead of having me lug it all back to my room, they offered to bring it by. Food, drinks, and the employees were wonderful, and you really got the feel of staying at a close friend's house.Additionally, I spent two nights at another property owned by Wind Chimes Inn, Casa del Caribe. It was a bit smaller. No bar or pool; although, we were allowed to go to the Wind Chimes Inn and use their facilities. This quaint BB had a nice veranda with a little fish pond, and a couple of cockateels in a big bird cage. It was very relaxing, and the rooms were tasteful and so comfortable. The staff was extremely helpful. For example, when our flight was cancelled, they were able to accomodate us for another night. Casa del Caribe is located close to the Marriot in Condado, so we spent time at the beach bar there. Plus, there was a great Sushi place nearby, as well as an awesome tapas bar, Miro's. The prices were extremely reasonable, leaving us more money to eat, drink, and enjoy our vacation even more. I would highly recommend these two properties.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Unpleasant Surprise My boyfriend and I went to Puerto Rico in December of 2004 and stayed at The Wind Chimes Inn for six nights. We chose this hotel after reading various positive reviews but were very disappointed during our stay.The night we checked in, the desk clerk requested my credit card. I gave it to her thinking that she wanted to confirm the number. Much to my surprise she charged us for the hotel fee that had been paid well in advance! Although she voided the transaction, I could not use my credit card for the remainder of the trip because it takes three business days (we arrived on a Friday night) for a transaction to be cancelled. Then the clerk told us that we would still have to pay an electricity fee that was not included in the bill! Since we were exhausted we decided not to argue with this woman and wait until the following day. Another staff member took us to our room but he refused to help us with our luggage because he had injured his back after helping guests whose bags were too heavy.Our room did not look like the pictures we had seen online. It was smaller, it didn't have a kichenette, the bathroom had no door and the bath tub was dirty. We also realized that the sheets were stained. Also, the phone in our room and the pay phone in the lobby were out of order three times in less than a week.On our last day at this hotel we found a cock roach under our bed and a rat was wandering around in the bar. We DO NOT recommend this hotel! There are much better places in San Juan.

On our return to hotel still before the 2 pm check in, we were given our room key and parking lot gate opener and was escourted to our room. It was just as the web site pictures showed. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel with Location, Location, Location We just returned from a stay in Puerto Rico April 14, 2005! We stayed at a guest house At Wind Chimes Inn that offers great personalized service. You can pay $300.00 at a larger hotel chain, but for the internet price of $99.00 for a queen size bed, you can't beat this. Realize you are in Puerto Rico and the rooms are nothing fancy, but comfortable. What makes this hotel is it's location and the friendly staff. They also have a bar just for hotel patrons and it's very reasonably priced for drinks in comparison to other places. We recommend four fabulous restaurants, each offereing the best of Puerto Rico. First, Tantra in old San Juan - the Mofongo is to die for and the Black Love Martini - a real winner in the asian fusion type cooking style. Second, Al Dente in Old San Juan - an excellent Italian Restaurant - quaint and intimate like Tantra but of course a different flavor - italian. We had the calamari with tartar sauce - it was outstanding and would have like to eat dinner there but already had plans. Service at this restaurant was impeccable. Lastly, an little Mexican place recommended to us that we absolutely loved. It's called Celito Lindo and it's on Calle Magdelene just past the Marriott J.W. and one street away from the ocean. It's next to the U.S. Post Office. At first glance and even entrance you might be a little unsure, but hold with it - fabulous food for a very reasonable price! We ordered the black bean soup and a combination plate (Number 3) and couldn't have enjoyed ourselves more. Simple, but good mexican food made from scratch. Lastly, for breakfast and just up the street from At Wind Chimes Inn is La Patisserie - they have $3.99 breakfast specials each day, look for the sign at the entrance of the restaurant (lunch specials also). We ordered the standard $4.95 breakfast, but it wasn't so standard - it was delicious served with potatoes (some spice I couldn't quite figure out) and french baguette with french toast, bacon, and eggs. A real bargain and stays with you all day. Enjoy!  
<Date>Apr 14, 2005

<Author>TimothyPT
<Content>Good for the Price A nice small hotel and VERY close to an uncrowded beach area. A 10 min walk to where all the action is but if you prefer to stay in the heart of it all go further into Condado area (although prices can be twice as much there). The bar staff was a bit distant and unfriendly. We were often greeted by a simple Yes. No hello what can I get you, etc. But they prepared a nice breakfast  lunch.Check-in was NOT good. We used a travel agent and the staff insisted on us providing some sort of voucher. It took a few min to convince him we do not have such a thing and he then realized it was not necessary if reservation was made through an agent. A good spot to spend the night before or after a cruise. Gay guests seemed welcome and was a 2 mile cab ride to popular dance club.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>nice place pros:-nice 'botique' feel. quaint hotel-helpful staff; good with directions and called for a taxi when we needed one-good smoothies at the bar-terra cotta decor-if you do stay in the annex building (see below) there is a nice roof deck with a full bathroom next to it, along with a somewhat obstructed view of the oceancons:-do not expect a resort or a large hotel with lots of staff, breakfasts, or even phones in the rooms-you may be relegated to their annex building (make sure of where you are staying) ... the annex building is a half a block closer to the beach, but it doesn't have the amenities of their main building (such as ice machine, bar-though they are building one-, front desk staff, pool)-very small pool in main building-$15.00 electricity fee (i think this may be a standard, but who knows)-small tvs (13in)-not at the 'heart' of condado per se. there is a 10 minute walk to where 'everything is' in condado, such as casinos, restaurants, little shops, etc.(a hotel like the radisson is in the heart of condado)-------places to eat at condado: take a cab to the other end of ashford and go to the 'Waikiki' for some shell steak (eat at the back)other places: Metropol for local food (isla verde); Dragonfly for fusion food (old san juan); this lone seafood place near the El conquistador hotel away from all the rest. it's towards the seven seas beach. get the red snapper!*feel free to contact me about this hotel! :)

<Author>hollywoodChicago
<Content>Positive and Negative We just returned from a three night stay, pre cruise, at the Inn. Positives about the Inn: Very clean, expert housekeeping and friendly staff. Location near the beach and nightlife is good. 25 cent bus ride to Old San Juan is a great value and fun. Bebo's restaurant, don't miss it. A full breakfast for two will cost about $10.00. The Inn arranged a trip to the rain forest with Hector, from Eco tours. He was great. If you do this tour ask for him. Our king corner room was bright and tastefully decorated. However, from previous reviews there seems to be a disparity among the rooms. We didn't use the pool, but it appeared clean. The pictures on the internet correctly depict the Inn.Negatives from our perspective: The Inn sits on a busy street (Mc Cleary). We stayed the weekend and the street noise (motorcycles, loud music from the bar and dogs barking) kept me awake most of the night. True, we could have turned on the air conditioning, but that was also noisy. Because the weather was not too hot I preferred to sleep with the windows open. The food at the bar was overpriced and not too good. I have never seen an omelet made on a George Foreman grill before! Go to Bebo's. This Inn is a good value compared to the overpriced hotels on the island, so if you don't mind the noise I would recommend it. Had it not been for the noise I would have given it an Excellent rating.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great boutique hotel This hotel is nice. We just came back from Puerto Rico and managed to squeeze one night at the WindChimes. The only problem I found is that when you try to make a reservation online or over the phone, they demand you reserve for 3 consecutive nights. However, once I was there they were able to accomodate us. I got a guest room with all the ammenities that I needed. It's not luxurious, but for the reasonable price you get a clean room, fresh towels, clean sheets, and cable... The bartender was great. She gave us suggestions of the hot spots in old San Juan. The staff was very helpful and the security of the place was top notch. You needed a key to come in and out of the gates. I would recommend this hotel, especially for single women. It's 5 minutes away from Isla Verde and 15 minutes away from old San Juan. There are several places to eat within walking distance. The pool was of good size, however, it was a bit chilly to dip in.. It's February.....  Try Bebo's Restaurant, is just a 5 minute walk from the hotel... and enjoy typical Puerto Rican cuisine... Also, try the bar at the hotel...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a great place! We just returned from a seven night stay at the beautiful Wind Chimes Inn. What a great place! Location was perfect just a block away from the open beach of Condado. With only 22 rooms the hotel is very peaceful and personal. The staff must rate amongst the most profesional and attentive at any hotel I've ever stayed at: perfect, helpful, and pleasant: Yuan, Murcia, Lynette, and of course, Gabby -always smiling. Their recommendations on restaurants was accurate and excellent. Their special treatment made us feel right at home. They sure do an excellent work on operating this hotel - on duty 24/7! The room we stayed in was perfect, the bed was perhaps the most comfortable of any hotel bed I've ever slept in. There was a lovely terrace with a small fountain where to enjoy some quiet reading and cocktails. I absolutely loved this hotel, and we agreed that we will never stay anywhere else in Puerto Rico again.During our stay, we encountered so many other guests who were enjoying their stay as well. Some were staying at another building down the street called the annex (or was it the akacia?), well, in all they loved this annex. I heard some of these rooms have balconies with a nice view. We would ask for these rooms next time. After a long day's sightseeing or shopping the courtyard boat bar is a joy to come back to for a cool, relaxing drink away from the madding crowds! Ask Dany or Rafy for a painkiller or a frozen margarita. Their service was excellent!

<Content>Thumbs up My husband and I were at the Wind Chimes from Nov. 14 - 27, 2004. I booked on-line and there was no choice in rooms. Upon arrival I asked for an upgrade and we were accomodated the next day. We stayed at the additional house which looked to be still in progress 1/2 block down the road  closer to the beach. Rooms were somewhat small but very clean and nicely furnished. The bathromm was also in good condition. Both rooms were kept in imacioulous conditions by the cleaning staff during our stay. The gated doors of that house were kept closed (guests had a key) and we felt safe and comfy there. We checked out the breakfast bar twice. The first time was great. A German lady most efficient and very friendly served us a sumptious breakfast. On our last morning, our second breakfast, it was a little less uplifting  mix-up in the order, missing food item, food came at different times for my husband and myselve etc. We were served by 2 people of which one said he didn't do the breakfast bar for a while and the second one spoke Spanish only and was just given instructions. So Ok Breakast bar was soso. Parking is a problem. Not many spaces and you have to make reservation otherwise you find yourselve circleling the blocks. The pool was a dissapointment. It looked nice in the pictures but turned out to be just a little more than a bath tup. The staff at the reception/concierge desk was fantastic. Always extremely helpfull and really friendly and sincere. Thumbs way up for these ladies. THANK YOU!!! To the neighorhood. At first it looked a little run down which it was. But for the people in the stores and restaurants they were warm and friendly to us tourists and made us feel ok and safe. No problem there. Buses are readily accessable and a bargain for 25 cents just one block off the hotel. No need for taxis. The beach looked nice and clean and hardly anybody enjoying it at the time we were there. For somebody who doesn't like the hype of the big hotel chains this hotel is perfect. It's clean, quite, private and everything is easily accessable. Also, Puerto Ricans are special people. Respect and kindness is in full swing. That's what we have experienced at our stay at this lovely island. My husbad and I are 48 and 54 years young of mixed race and culture and like to do things our way especially on our vacation. We hate to be put on a schedule or box, or told when to do and what to wear or being insulted or disrespected by other guests or anybody or anything for that matter. PEACE

<Author>clm2006
<Content>Nice but not FABULOUS There is a lot going right at Wind Chimes. My family and I were there for 13 days. It's a lovely place, lots of charm and intimacy, beautiful physical plant and the people running the place (Gaby especially, who was so accommodating to our needs and helpful with advice about where to eat and how to get here or there.) are fantastic. The location can't be beat. A four minute walk from the beach and at the perfect spot to pick up the central highways on the island. There are great restaurants within walking distance (Bebo's, Kasalta) and if you don't have a car, public transportation can be picked up close by as well. I felt safe there...but I wasn't in the annex, which sounded a little fishy to me when it was mentioned when I first called. It's not completed and I think they're using it eariler than they should. Here's what could be better at Wind Chimes: pool hours are too short (9-6); the pool is TINY! Literally four people max can move in that space. And as for the jacuzzi, uh...it's more like pool pumps that you can press your back against. ANd the last two days we were there, the pool was developing a disturbing cloudiness that no one seemed to see fit to apologize for or explain. There is no complimentary breakfast...even continental could do the trick, especially when the place bills itself as welcoming for kids. A family can't plunk down 8 bucks a day for a bowl of cereal and a glass of juice, which is what you'd spend at the Tikki Bar at Wind Chimes. The room attendants make the beds and refresh towels, but don't reliably sweep the gritty sand that inevitably comes in on your sandals, nor do they re-supply the shampoo unless you ask. There's no iron in the room, which one might need if one were doing business on the island and needed pressed clothing. They supply beach towels, but could think about renting out beach umbrellas, especially since they bill themselves as having access to the beach. One cannot just sit there and roast all day without serious damage taking place. The parking facilities are horrible. There are about five spaces and you have to park about an inch from a wall in order to fit, so if you're not ready or able to climb out of the opposite door, you're stuck. I'm getting a little too crickety to have to climb out of a car. So, the bottom line is, it's a cozy, reliable, safe, convenient, and pleasant place to stay in PR. I'd stay there again if I needed to. I'd recommend it to people. BUT, I will look around for another place in the Condado area for the next time I head to Borinquen--just to see if there's something better.  
<Date>Aug 8, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't go here if you can afford not to.. YOU GET WHAT YOU PAY FOR! We were very disappointed after so many glowing reports and recommendations. The first big problem was the parking. We paid extra for a reserved parking spot and the parking lot turned out to be a tiny area that looked like an alley. We spent the week maneuvering in and out with the other cars hoping not to hit a wall or other car. You are forced to back out of the alley onto a busy street.We had reserved what was supposed to be a renovated room (Like those on the website). The first room they showed us had broken tile on the floor, paint peeling in the bath, a tiny TV, and a window which would not close (not good for the bugs). The second room they gave us was even smaller (Think walk through the door and hit the foot of the bed) but in a bit better shape.Though we downgraded, we weren't offered a lower price or any apology. The showers were nothing more than a corner of the bathroom with a shower head covered by a curtain. It wasn't particularly clean or quiet. It was a bother to have to open a lock to get OUT of the place! The pool closed at 6 p.m. (when you'd like to get IN). Don't go by the website--we were surprised at the exaggerations. Not a wind chime in the place! But for the price we paid, about half of what we'd have paid at a large hotel, it was OK. Didn't feel particularly safe but not in danger, either. The staff was friendly. I saw that you should make VERY CLEAR what kind of room you want and be ready to accept the bare bones. The beach was gorgeous but the walk there is through a seedy neighborhood. If you have the money, go elsewhere . If we go back to PR, we will go elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good but is it safe? My wife and I enjoyed the ambiance,friendly bar staff, close proximity to a beautiful beach, and general cleanliness of this boutique hotel, but were surprised and saddened to have a bag full of souveniers stolen from our room. The rooms and front gate all have the same key in the newly renovated annex (as does the main hotel ) but the annex has no security at the gate. Our room also had no phone in it, and the light in the hall was out and was never fixed during the 5 days we stayed despite telling them numerous times.The manager and staff were considerate and showed concern regarding the theft but ultimately did nothing ( not even a complementary drink!) about it. The bar/restaurant is very good for a kitchen that consists of a George Foreman grill and refrigerator, and the concierges were helpful with reservations etc.Your stay in San Juan should be a safe one,so be on your guard and don't leave valuable in your room.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We loved it! We stayed in the Wind Chimes Inn this past April. All of the hotels and condos were booked so we couldn't find anything and this was the only place that had any vacancy. Lucky for us, or else we would have never known about this place. The hotel is small, quaint and cozy. So if you like those big crowded resorts, this is not the hotel for you! The atmosphere is permeated with a rich incense smell that gives it an even more homey feel. In fact, it feels just like a big house, with its personal touches of art and those quirky turtle shaped lights on the steps. We got the junior suite that had its own terrace and made us feel like we had our own wing. It was not fancy by any means, with its wicker furniture and basic amenities, but it was clean and comfortable. The decor was bright and tropical, and the art reflected the local flavor. The staff was very helpful, especially when I needed new linens at 3 am, thanks to my son, they really took good care of me. My old linens were taken by housekeeping early the next morning, from where I had laid them to dry on the terrace. We had a nice visit with some friends on that terrace and it felt like we were at home. The pool, albeit small, felt like our very own pool. It wasn't crowded with rowdy children; in fact we were the rowdy ones in comparison to the quiet sunbathers and novel-reading sun lovers. The courtyard is adorable and really added to the bed-and-breakfast feel of the small quaint inn. The only downside is the lack of parking and the difficulty in getting in when you first arrive but that is for our own safety, so I could deal with that. Plus it's close to town where we could walk and get anything we needed. We did our laundry and picked up some odds and ends. It was close to Bebo's, where you could have a nice, affordable sit down meal. It was close to anything you needed, really. I preferred walking as parking was at such a premium, once I found a spot, I didn't want to move my car. However, the area was very secure and the car was safe.We loved it here so much that we are going back on our return visit in October. No matter what, we said, we had to get in at least one night at The Wind Chimes. I'm recommending it to everyone who wants a recommendation on a nice hotel, that feels like home without the frills and expense and crowd of a big resort.  
<Date>Jul 7, 2004
